## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The variables describe a single population P evolving over time t, with the target dP_dt indicating a governing differential equation for population growth. Common models relate growth rate to density dependence (functions of P) and/or time-varying environment (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant net input/immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (birth-death plus constant immigration)
- Logistic (Verhulst) differential form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (linear density dependence; c1 ~ 1/K)
- Generalized logistic (Richards / P-theta): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (tunable curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz differential form: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (when written as log(P/K) with constants absorbed; multiplicative log-density regulation)
- Allee effect (strong) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low density plus saturation at high density)
- Allee effect (weak) rational form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) / (P + c2) (low-density inhibition with smooth transition)
- Density-dependent mortality (quadratic loss): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding/competition-induced losses)
- Harvesting/constant removal: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed-yield harvest pressure)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (effort proportional to population size)
- Time-varying per-capita rate (trend): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (changing environment or management over time)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environmental forcing)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (1 + c2 * exp(-c3 * t))) (capacity shifts over time; constants kept multiplicative)
- Self-limitation with time forcing in loss term: dP_dt = c0 * P - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * P**2 (seasonal crowding/competition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth rate r(P,t) = dP_dt / P being approximately constant suggests dP_dt ∝ P (exponential regime).
- Linear decrease of per-capita growth with P suggests logistic structure: dP_dt = P * (a - b * P).
- If growth is suppressed at low P (possible critical threshold), include an Allee factor like (P - c) or (P - c)/(P + c).
- If regulation acts multiplicatively on log-density (e.g., size-dependent proportional feedback), terms like P * log(c*P) (Gompertz-type) are typical.
- Seasonal or cyclic environments produce sinusoidal modulation of coefficients: (a + b*sin(ω*t+φ)) multiplying P and/or P^2.
- Long-term environmental change (e.g., gradual resource decline/improvement) often appears as coefficients that drift with time: (a + b*t) or a + b*exp(-c*t).
- Harvesting or culling introduces additive (constant) removal terms (-c) or proportional removal (-c*P), distinguishable by how dP_dt behaves near P ≈ 0.
- If growth rate becomes strongly negative at high P, higher-order density dependence (e.g., -P^m with m>2) can capture sharp crowding effects.
- If data show an upper bound that itself changes over time, model time-dependent carrying capacity via rational/exponential-in-t modifiers inside (1 - P/K(t)).

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG19)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P/t**c4
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):  
\[
0.4205670824\,(1-\tfrac{P}{84.41334764})P \;+\; 0.4205670824\,\frac{P}{t^{2.594538327}}
\]
Rewrite GT as a sum of a pure-in-\(P\) quadratic polynomial plus a separable \(P\cdot t^{-k}\) term:
\[
\underbrace{0.4205670824\,P - \frac{0.4205670824}{84.41334764}P^2}_{\text{depends only on }P}
\;+\;
\underbrace{0.4205670824\,P\,t^{-2.594538327}}_{\text{product }P\cdot f(t)}
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **(i)** a \(P^2\) term and a \(P\) term with fixed coefficients, and **(ii)** an additional term exactly of the form \(P/t^{2.5945...}\) (no extra \(t\)-only terms, no logs/exp/sin in \(P\), no \(1/t\) unless multiplied by \(P\), etc.).

Now check candidates:

1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 t^{c3} + c4\log(Pc5+1)\).  
   The needed \(P/t^k\) would require \(Pc2 t^{c3}\) with \(c3=-2.5945...\). Possible. But the log term must vanish: set \(c4=0\). Then we can set \(c0=-0.420567/84.4133\), \(c1=0.420567\), \(c2=0.420567\), \(c3=-2.594538...\). **Matches.**

2. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P t^{c2} + c3 t^{c4} + c5 t^{c6}\log(c7 t+1)\).  
   Can make \(Pt^{c2}=P/t^{2.5945}\) by \(c2=-2.5945\). Need to kill the last two \(t\)-only terms for all \(t\): set \(c3=0\) and \(c5=0\). Then choose \(c0,c1\) as above. **Matches.**

3. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P t^{c2} + c3 t^{c4}\).  
   Same: set \(c2=-2.5945\), set \(c3=0\), choose \(c0,c1\) to match polynomial part, and coefficient of \(Pt^{c2}\) is fixed at 1 here (no constant multiplier). GT needs coefficient \(0.420567...\). There is no free multiplier on \(P t^{c2}\). So cannot match unless \(0.420567=1\), impossible. **No match.**
